primarily in the `dom/events` directory with central coordination through `EventDispatcher`. A DOM event (e.g., click) follows a well-defined path through event creation, target identification, capture/bubble phase traversal, listener invocation, and default action execution.\\n\\n## Event Creation\\nWhen an event is dispatched, it starts in **EventDispatcher::Dispatch()** (dom/events/EventDispatcher.cpp, line 869). The method accepts a WidgetEvent (low-level platform event) or DOM Event. If needed, a DOM Event is created via **EventDispatcher::CreateEvent()** (dom/events/EventDispatcher.cpp, line 1234), which wraps the WidgetEvent in an appropriate DOM Event class (e.g., MouseEvent, ClickEvent, etc.).\\n\\n## Event Target Chain Identification\\nAfter event creation, an event target chain is built by starting with the initial target and repeatedly calling **GetEventTargetParent()** on each target. This process occurs in **EventDispatcher::Dispatch()** (starting around line 1008) where:\\n\\n1. **EventTargetChainItem::Create()** creates the first chain item for the initial target (line 1009)\\n2. The system calls **GetEventTargetParent()** on the current target through the **EventTargetChainItem** class (line 1063)\\n3. **EventTarget::GetEventTargetParent()** (dom/events/EventTarget.h, line 282) is a virtual method that subclasses implement to identify their parent targets\\n4. Chain building continues until either no parent target exists or **mCanHandle** becomes false\\n5. This creates a complete path from the deepest child element to the document root\\n\\nKey visitor class: **EventChainPreVisitor** (dom/events/EventDispatcher.h, line 113) tracks state during chain construction, including flags for event retargeting and special handling requirements.\\n\\n## Capture/Bubble Phase Traversal\\nThe actual event dispatching occurs in **EventTargetChainItem::HandleEventTargetChain()** (dom/events/EventDispatcher.cpp, line 491), which implements the three-phase event dispatch model:\\n\\n### Capture Phase (line 516-585)\\n- Sets flags: `mInCapturePhase = true`, `mInBubblingPhase = false`\\n- Iterates from the top of the chain down to the target (from parent to child)\\n- Calls **item.HandleEvent()** on each chain item if conditions are met (line 528)\\n- Event propagation can be stopped by checking **PropagationStopped()**\\n\\n### Target Phase (line 587-611)\\n- Sets `mInTargetPhase = true`\\n- Handles the target element itself\\n- Calls **HandleEvent()** twice: once in capture mode, once in bubble mode\\n- After target phase in system group, calls **PostHandleEvent()** (line 609)\\n\\n### Bubble Phase (line 613-649)\\n- Sets `mInBubblingPhase = true`, `mInCapturePhase = false`\\n- Iterates from the target upward through the chain (from child to parent)\\n- Only processes if event has `mBubbles` flag set (line 638)\\n- Calls **PostHandleEvent()** for system group listeners (line 645)\\n\\n## Event Listener Invocation\\nWhen **EventTargetChainItem::HandleEvent()** (dom/events/EventDispatcher.cpp, line 339) is called, it retrieves the event listener manager from the target and delegates to **EventListenerManager::HandleEvent()** (dom/events/EventListenerManager.h, line 435).\\n\\nThe listener invocation chain works as follows:\\n\\n1. **EventListenerManager::HandleEvent()** (line 435) performs fast-path checks to skip processing if:\\n   - No capturing listeners and not in bubbling phase\\n   - No system group listeners but event is in system group\\n   - Untrusted event but no listeners accept untrusted events\\n   - Listener map is empty\\n\\n2. **EventListenerManager::HandleEventInternal()** (dom/events/EventListenerManager.cpp, line 1439) does the actual work:\\n   - Checks for \\\"all events\\\" listeners first (line 1481)\\n   - Gets listeners for the specific event type atom (line 1491)\\n   - Calls **HandleEventWithListenerArray()** for each listener set (line 1493)\\n\\n3. **EventListenerManager::HandleEventWithListenerArray()** (line 1536) iterates through all listeners:\\n   - Creates DOM Event on-demand if not already created (line 1581)\\n   - Filters listeners by phase (capture vs. bubble) and event trustedness\\n   - Handles \\\"once\\\" listeners by removing them before invocation\\n   - Calls **HandleEventSingleListener()** for each matching listener\\n\\n4. **EventListenerManager::HandleEventSingleListener()** (line 1233) actually invokes the listener:\\n   - Sets up the event's currentTarget (line 1237)\\n   - Compiles JavaScript event handlers if needed (line 1261)\\n   - For WebIDL callbacks, calls **listenerHolder.GetWebIDLCallback()->HandleEvent()** (line 1276)\\n   - For XPCOM listeners, calls **listenerHolder.GetXPCOMCallback()->HandleEvent()** (line 1281)\\n   - Handles listener exceptions and returns whether propagation should continue (line 1294)\\n\\n## Default Action Execution\\nAfter the system event group completes, default actions are executed through the activation behavior mechanism:\\n\\n1. **EventDispatcher::Dispatch()** checks if an activation target was set during event chain construction (line 1334)\\n2. If the event wasn't prevented, **chain[activationTargetItemIndex].ActivationBehavior()** is called (line 1340)\\n3. **EventTarget::ActivationBehavior()** (dom/events/EventTarget.h, line 295) is a virtual method that elements implement\\n4. Concrete implementations exist in:\\n   - **HTMLInputElement::ActivationBehavior()** (dom/html/HTMLInputElement.cpp, line 4299) - handles form submission, button clicks\\n   - **HTMLButtonElement::ActivationBehavior()** (dom/html/HTMLButtonElement.cpp, line 315) - handles button clicks and form submission\\n5. If the event was prevented with preventDefault(), **LegacyCanceledActivationBehavior()** is called instead (line 1337)\\n\\n## Post-Event Processing\\nAfter all event phases:\\n\\n1. **EventTargetChainItem::PostHandleEvent()** (dom/events/EventDispatcher.cpp, line 483) is called during system group processing\\n2. Calls **EventTarget::PostHandleEvent()** (dom/events/EventTarget.h, line 326), a virtual method for post-processing\\n3. **EventStateManager::PostHandleEvent()** (dom/events/EventStateManager.cpp, line 3977) performs browser-level default actions:\\n   - Focus management\\n   - Selection changes\\n   - UI state updates\\n   - Context menu handling\\n4. The event's target and related targets are cleared if appropriate (line 1326)\\n5. Event's `mDispatchedAtLeastOnce` flag is set (line 1316)\\n\\n## Key Design Patterns\\n\\n### Visitor Pattern\\nThe system uses visitor objects (`EventChainPreVisitor`, `EventChainPostVisitor`) to pass state through the chain without modifying the chain items directly. This allows each target to communicate information up the chain during construction and back down during dispatch.\\n\\n### Event Retargeting\\nShadow DOM and anonymous content requires event retargeting. The `EventChainPreVisitor` tracks `mEventTargetAtParent` to handle cases where the event target changes as it crosses shadow boundaries.\\n\\n### Event Groups\\nFirefox supports two event groups: default (content) and system (browser internals). The system group runs after the default group, allowing browser code to handle events after JavaScript has processed them.\\n\\n### Listener Type Support\\nThe system supports three listener types:\\n- WebIDL EventListener callbacks (JavaScript addEventListener)\\n- XPCOM nsIDOMEventListener (native Firefox code)\\n- Compiled JavaScript event handlers (onX attributes)\\n\\nThis architecture enables efficient, spec-compliant event handling with browser-level customizations while maintaining a clean separation between event dispatching, listener management, and default action execution.\"\n}\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":12,"cache_creation_input_tokens":7131,"cache_read_input_tokens":91591,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":7131},"output_tokens":1,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"5751abb9-c4e5-4b38-9e21-ab45d2ea5740","uuid":"07c94147-92ac-49fd-8d6a-5e38e862bf95"}

\"symbol\": \"EventTargetChainItem::PostHandleEvent\"\n    }\n  ],\n  \"text\": \"# Firefox DOM Event Dispatch Chain Analysis\\n\\n## Overview\\nThe Firefox event dispatch system is implemented primarily in the `dom/events` directory with central coordination through `EventDispatcher`. A DOM event (e.g., click) follows a well-defined path through event creation, target identification, capture/bubble phase traversal, listener invocation, and default action execution.\\n\\n## Event Creation\\nWhen an event is dispatched, it starts in **EventDispatcher::Dispatch()** (dom/events/EventDispatcher.cpp, line 869). The method accepts a WidgetEvent (low-level platform event) or DOM Event. If needed, a DOM Event is created via **EventDispatcher::CreateEvent()** (dom/events/EventDispatcher.cpp, line 1234), which wraps the WidgetEvent in an appropriate DOM Event class (e.g., MouseEvent, ClickEvent, etc.).\\n\\n## Event Target Chain Identification\\nAfter event creation, an event target chain is built by starting with the initial target and repeatedly calling **GetEventTargetParent()** on each target. This process occurs in **EventDispatcher::Dispatch()** (starting around line 1008) where:\\n\\n1. **EventTargetChainItem::Create()** creates the first chain item for the initial target (line 1009)\\n2. The system calls **GetEventTargetParent()** on the current target through the **EventTargetChainItem** class (line 1063)\\n3. **EventTarget::GetEventTargetParent()** (dom/events/EventTarget.h, line 282) is a virtual method that subclasses implement to identify their parent targets\\n4. Chain building continues until either no parent target exists or **mCanHandle** becomes false\\n5. This creates a complete path from the deepest child element to the document root\\n\\nKey visitor class: **EventChainPreVisitor** (dom/events/EventDispatcher.h, line 113) tracks state during chain construction, including flags for event retargeting and special handling requirements.\\n\\n## Capture/Bubble Phase Traversal\\nThe actual event dispatching occurs in **EventTargetChainItem::HandleEventTargetChain()** (dom/events/EventDispatcher.cpp, line 491), which implements the three-phase event dispatch model:\\n\\n### Capture Phase (line 516-585)\\n- Sets flags: `mInCapturePhase = true`, `mInBubblingPhase = false`\\n- Iterates from the top of the chain down to the target (from parent to child)\\n- Calls **item.HandleEvent()** on each chain item if conditions are met (line 528)\\n- Event propagation can be stopped by checking **PropagationStopped()**\\n\\n### Target Phase (line 587-611)\\n- Sets `mInTargetPhase = true`\\n- Handles the target element itself\\n- Calls **HandleEvent()** twice: once in capture mode, once in bubble mode\\n- After target phase in system group, calls **PostHandleEvent()** (line 609)\\n\\n### Bubble Phase (line 613-649)\\n- Sets `mInBubblingPhase = true`, `mInCapturePhase = false`\\n- Iterates from the target upward through the chain (from child to parent)\\n- Only processes if event has `mBubbles` flag set (line 638)\\n- Calls **PostHandleEvent()** for system group listeners (line 645)\\n\\n## Event Listener Invocation\\nWhen **EventTargetChainItem::HandleEvent()** (dom/events/EventDispatcher.cpp, line 339) is called, it retrieves the event listener manager from the target and delegates to **EventListenerManager::HandleEvent()** (dom/events/EventListenerManager.h, line 435).\\n\\nThe listener invocation chain works as follows:\\n\\n1. **EventListenerManager::HandleEvent()** (line 435) performs fast-path checks to skip processing if:\\n   - No capturing listeners and not in bubbling phase\\n   - No system group listeners but event is in system group\\n   - Untrusted event but no listeners accept untrusted events\\n   - Listener map is empty\\n\\n2. **EventListenerManager::HandleEventInternal()** (dom/events/EventListenerManager.cpp, line 1439) does the actual work:\\n   - Checks for \\\"all events\\\" listeners first (line 1481)\\n   - Gets listeners for the specific event type atom (line 1491)\\n   - Calls **HandleEventWithListenerArray()** for each listener set (line 1493)\\n\\n3. **EventListenerManager::HandleEventWithListenerArray()** (line 1536) iterates through all listeners:\\n   - Creates DOM Event on-demand if not already created (line 1581)\\n   - Filters listeners by phase (capture vs. bubble) and event trustedness\\n   - Handles \\\"once\\\" listeners by removing them before invocation\\n   - Calls **HandleEventSingleListener()** for each matching listener\\n\\n4. **EventListenerManager::HandleEventSingleListener()** (line 1233) actually invokes the listener:\\n   - Sets up the event's currentTarget (line 1237)\\n   - Compiles JavaScript event handlers if needed (line 1261)\\n   - For WebIDL callbacks, calls **listenerHolder.GetWebIDLCallback()->HandleEvent()** (line 1276)\\n   - For XPCOM listeners, calls **listenerHolder.GetXPCOMCallback()->HandleEvent()** (line 1281)\\n   - Handles listener exceptions and returns whether propagation should continue (line 1294)\\n\\n## Default Action Execution\\nAfter the system event group completes, default actions are executed through the activation behavior mechanism:\\n\\n1. **EventDispatcher::Dispatch()** checks if an activation target was set during event chain construction (line 1334)\\n2. If the event wasn't prevented, **chain[activationTargetItemIndex].ActivationBehavior()** is called (line 1340)\\n3. **EventTarget::ActivationBehavior()** (dom/events/EventTarget.h, line 295) is a virtual method that elements implement\\n4. Concrete implementations exist in:\\n   - **HTMLInputElement::ActivationBehavior()** (dom/html/HTMLInputElement.cpp, line 4299) - handles form submission, button clicks\\n   - **HTMLButtonElement::ActivationBehavior()** (dom/html/HTMLButtonElement.cpp, line 315) - handles button clicks and form submission\\n5. If the event was prevented with preventDefault(), **LegacyCanceledActivationBehavior()** is called instead (line 1337)\\n\\n## Post-Event Processing\\nAfter all event phases:\\n\\n1. **EventTargetChainItem::PostHandleEvent()** (dom/events/EventDispatcher.cpp, line 483) is called during system group processing\\n2. Calls **EventTarget::PostHandleEvent()** (dom/events/EventTarget.h, line 326), a virtual method for post-processing\\n3. **EventStateManager::PostHandleEvent()** (dom/events/EventStateManager.cpp, line 3977) performs browser-level default actions:\\n   - Focus management\\n   - Selection changes\\n   - UI state updates\\n   - Context menu handling\\n4. The event's target and related targets are cleared if appropriate (line 1326)\\n5. Event's `mDispatchedAtLeastOnce` flag is set (line 1316)\\n\\n## Key Design Patterns\\n\\n### Visitor Pattern\\nThe system uses visitor objects (`EventChainPreVisitor`, `EventChainPostVisitor`) to pass state through the chain without modifying the chain items directly. This allows each target to communicate information up the chain during construction and back down during dispatch.\\n\\n### Event Retargeting\\nShadow DOM and anonymous content requires event retargeting. The `EventChainPreVisitor` tracks `mEventTargetAtParent` to handle cases where the event target changes as it crosses shadow boundaries.\\n\\n### Event Groups\\nFirefox supports two event groups: default (content) and system (browser internals). The system group runs after the default group, allowing browser code to handle events after JavaScript has processed them.\\n\\n### Listener Type Support\\nThe system supports three listener types:\\n- WebIDL EventListener callbacks (JavaScript addEventListener)\\n- XPCOM nsIDOMEventListener (native Firefox code)\\n- Compiled JavaScript event handlers (onX attributes)\\n\\nThis architecture enables efficient, spec-compliant event handling with browser-level customizations while maintaining a clean separation between event dispatching, listener management, and default action execution.\"\n}\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}
